Mr. Mosley is a Word War II veteran and is one of the only living survivors of the 87 Aggies who served in the Philippines.\n\nDuring the war, Mr. Mosely was captured by the Japanese and heroically survived the Bataan Death March in April 1942, where he was later held at the infamous Cabanatuan prisoner of war camp, and was then transferred to the POW camp in Mukden, Manchuria in October 1942\u2014where he remained until liberated at the war's end on August 20, 1945. \n\nIn an effort to raise the morale of the POW camp, Mr. Mosely illustrated the camp newsletter, similar to that of his 1938 Battalion illustration, which depicts a cadet traveling home for the holidays. Blanketed in snow and wrapped in an overcoat and scarf while puffing on a pipe with one hand in his pocket and the other outreached in a familiar \u201cGig \u2018em\u201d sign, the cadet patiently thumbs a ride home. The Aggie \u201cGig \u2018em\u201d moniker and hand-sign, already popularized in 1938, was also a common gesture for hitch-hiking, or thumbing, which was a common method of transportation for Texas A&M students in the 1920s through 1960s.  \n#AgLibLove", "type": "photo", "id": "102337189813993_625802947467412", "status_type": "added_photos", "icon": "https://static.xx.fbcdn.net/rsrc.php/v2/yz/r/StEh3RhPvjk.gif"}

If I find the 1940s Batt I will get to you soon as I can.", "id": "539321442782230_1628147", "user_likes": false}, {"from": {"name": "Pam Johnson", "id": "100001043174947"}, "like_count": 2, "can_remove": false, "created_time": "2013-06-16T15:43:46+0000", "message": "When I was writing my 2 Aggie history books, David Chapman showed me this flag in its box (it was too fragile to be handled), and I was honored and thrilled. I inserted a short history of it in my book \"The Corps: The Core of A&M.\" In 1918, A&M students sewed the flag out of wool muslin in the students' tailor shop in the basement of the Academic Bldg. It measured 15 ft. by 26 ft. Inside its red border are 1,963 maroon stars, each representing a Texas A&M student or former student who served in WWI. In the center are 57 white stars, representing Aggies who died in the war. It was first raised 27 May 1918 in Guion Hall, where Rudder Center now stands. In the 1920s it was moved to the Academic Bldg where it hung until 1946 when the wool corners tore and the flag fell. Stored in a closet, it was forgotten until 1970 when James B. Jones, '71, found the flag when some old offices in the Academic Bldg were being cleaned out. He gave it to Dr. David Chapman, then with the A&M Archives at Cushing Library. David wanted to have a replica made in time for the 100th anniversary of WWI. I went to the flag-making place in San Antonio and asked if they could do it. It would have cost about $10-15,000 at the time.", "id": "539321442782230_1633006", "user_likes": false}, {"from": {"category": "Library", "name": "Texas A&M University Libraries", "id": "102337189813993"}, "like_count": 0, "can_remove": false, "created_time": "2013-06-17T14:46:51+0000", "message": "Thanks for sharing more of the story Pam!", "id": "539321442782230_1634592", "user_likes": false}, {"from": {"name": "Pam Johnson", "id": "100001043174947"}, "like_count": 0, "can_remove": false, "created_time": "2013-06-17T19:25:48+0000", "message": "You are welcome!
